   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d148370250" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Compared with the extensively used ester-based electrolyte, the hard carbon (HC) electrode is more compatible with the ether-based counterpart in sodium-ion batteries, which can lead to improved cycling stability and robust rate capability. However, the impact of salt anion on the electrochemical performance of HC electrodes has yet to be fully understood. In this study, the anionic chemistry in regulating the stability of electrolytes and the performance of sodium-ion batteries have been systematically investigated. This work shows discrepancies in the reductive stability of the anionic group, redox kinetics, and component/structure of solid electrolyte interface (SEI) with different salts (NaBF<sub>4,</sub> NaPF<sub>6</sub>, and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>) in the typical ether solvent (diglyme). Particularly, the density functional theory calculation manifests the preferred decomposition of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> due to the reduced reductive stability of anions in the solvation structure, thus leading to the formation of NaF-rich SEI. Further investigation on redox kinetics reveals that the NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme can induce the fast ionic diffusion dynamic and low charge transfer barrier for HC electrode, thus resulting in superior sodium storage performance in terms of rate capability and cycling life, which outperforms those of NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme. Importantly, this work offers valuable insights for optimizing the electrochemical behaviors of electrode materials by regulating the anionic group in the electrolyte.</p></div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="cey2518-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="cey2518-sec-0010-title">1 INTRODUCTION</h2>
         
         <p>In recent years, the rising cost of raw materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) has promoted the development of alternative technologies. Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have shown great promise for large-scale energy storage, given the elemental abundance of sodium and the comparable energy density and manufacturing processes to LIBs.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0001_R_d148370241e428" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Sci Adv">1</a>-<a href="#cey2518-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0003_R_d148370241e428" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Angew Chem Int Ed">3</a></sup></span> Regarding the electrode for SIBs, hard carbon (HC) has received significant attention owing to its acceptable cost and high energy output in full cells.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0004_R_d148370241e431" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Carbon Energy">4</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0005_R_d148370241e431" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Adv Mater">5</a></sup></span> The charge storage in HC can be separated into adsorption and intercalation processes, corresponding to the slope capacity above 0.1 V versus Na/Na<sup>+</sup> and subsequent plateau capacity below 0.1 V versus Na/Na<sup>+</sup>, respectively.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0006_R_d148370241e438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv Funct Mater">6</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0007_R_d148370241e438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Adv Funct Mater">7</a></sup></span> In principle, the capacity contributions from both regions are closely associated with bulk defects, pore structure, disordered stacks, and surface chemistry of HC.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0008_R_d148370241e442" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv Funct Mater">8</a></sup></span> Additionally, serious concentration polarization at high rates results in degradation of the plateau region, leading to poor cycling and rate capability.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0009_R_d148370241e445" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Energy Environ Mater">9</a></sup></span> To overcome these limitations, various structure modifications, such as heteroatom doping, closed pore fabrication, ordered domain adjustment, and surface optimization, have been utilized to create a well-defined and controlled structure that enhances the sodium storage performance of the HC electrode.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0010_R_d148370241e448" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Energy Storage Mater">10</a>-<a href="#cey2518-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0012_R_d148370241e448" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Energy Storage Mater">12</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>The performance of SIBs is also highly influenced by the compatibility of the electrode with the electrolyte and the properties of the associated solid electrolyte interphases (SEI).<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0013_R_d148370241e453" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Energy Stor Mater">13</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0014_R_d148370241e453" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - J Phys Chem C">14</a></sup></span> A favorable interaction between the electrode and electrolyte results in a stable and robust SEI that can efficiently prevent the continuous decomposition of electrolytes, achieve good ionic conductivity, and contribute to high electrochemical reversibility.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0015_R_d148370241e456" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Nano Energy">15</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0016_R_d148370241e456" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Nano Lett">16</a></sup></span> Thus, a reliable electrolyte is essential to regulating the electrochemical behavior and interphase structure for high-performance SIBs with fast-charging ability, high rate capability, and robust cycling stability.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0017_R_d148370241e459" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Nano Res">17</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0018_R_d148370241e459" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Small Methods">18</a></sup></span> Compared with the conventional ester-based electrolytes, the ether-based electrolytes with good chemical compatibility are advantageous for the HC electrode, resulting in favorable electrode/electrolyte interaction, superior electrochemical reversibility, and the formation of robust SEI layers abundant with inorganic species.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0003_R_d148370241e462" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Angew Chem Int Ed">3</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0008_R_d148370241e462" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv Funct Mater">8</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0019_R_d148370241e462" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Adv Mater Interfaces">19</a></sup></span> Recent work by Dong et al. has demonstrated a novel co-intercalation mechanism of solvated Na<sup>+</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup> in monodispersed HC nanospheres when ether-based electrolyte was used.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0005_R_d148370241e470" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Adv Mater">5</a></sup></span> Additionally,&nbsp;using an ether-based electrolyte, an ultrahigh initial Coulombic efficiency for the carbon anode has been reported by Zhang et al.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0020_R_d148370241e473" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Nano Energy">20</a></sup></span> A uniform, thin, compact, and ionically conducting SEI layer generated in these systems plays a critical role in achieving high performance.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0002_R_d148370241e476" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Nat Commun">2</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0021_R_d148370241e476" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Nat Commun">21</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0022_R_d148370241e476" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Nat Energy">22</a></sup></span> Accordingly, these inspired works have prompted extensive studies focusing on comparing the performance, mechanism, kinetics, and SEI components between ester-based electrolytes and their ether-based counterparts to achieve high-performance SIBs.</p>
         
         <p>Recent studies demonstrate that the Na<sup>+</sup> are solvated in electrolytes, and anionic groups are arranged out of the inner solvation sheath.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0023_R_d148370241e484" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Small">23</a>-<a href="#cey2518-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0025_R_d148370241e484" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Chem Soc Rev">25</a></sup></span> In the typical sodiation process, the solvated Na<sup>+</sup> migrates to the electrode-electrolyte interface and undergoes desolvation, intercalation, or adsorption, corresponding to the typical charge transfer process.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0026_R_d148370241e489" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Angew Chem Int Ed">26</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0027_R_d148370241e489" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Angew Chem Int Ed">27</a></sup></span> Meanwhile, the solvation sheath formed by solvent and anions can be reduced to form the SEI layer during initial electrochemical cycling, and the adjustment of solvent and anion in the electrolyte is believed to be efficient for the optimization of the SEI layer.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0026_R_d148370241e492" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Angew Chem Int Ed">26</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0028_R_d148370241e492" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Angew Chem Int Ed">28</a></sup></span> In view of this, the anionic group occupies the outer sheath of the solvation structure, which affects the ionic migration kinetics due to steric hindrance.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0024_R_d148370241e496" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem Sci">24</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0029_R_d148370241e496" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Chem Eng J">29</a></sup></span> Additionally, the various solvation structures, with different anionic groups, result in discrepancies in the SEI layer structure and components, which leads to electrochemical behaviors variations.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0030_R_d148370241e499" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Adv Energy Mater">30</a>-<a href="#cey2518-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0032_R_d148370241e499" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Nano-Micro Lett">32</a></sup></span> Nevertheless, the majority of studies focus on the influence of solvents in electrochemical behaviors, and less attention is paid to the effects of the anionic group on the stability of electrolyte, redox dynamics, energy barrier for charge transfer, and SEI component. Importantly, the understanding of the correlation among anionic chemistry, component/structure of the SEI layer, reaction kinetics, and electrochemical performance will facilitate rational electrolytes for building high-performance batteries.</p>
         
         <p>Herein, a systematic comparison of anionic groups on the electrochemical behavior of HC in ether-based electrolytes, aiming to clarify the correlation of anionic chemistry, redox kinetics, structure/component of SEI, and electrochemical sodium storage performance, has been performed. This involved using sodium hexafluorophosphate (NaPF<sub>6</sub>), sodium tetrafluoroborate (NaBF<sub>4</sub>), and sodium trifluoromethanesulfonate (NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>) as conducting salts, and diethylene glycol dimethyl ether (diglyme) as the typical ether solvent. The detailed investigation demonstrates that the preferred decomposition of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> induced an inorganic-rich SEI, satisfied ionic conductivity accompanied with high Na<sup>+</sup> transference number, and favorable redox kinetics of the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme. This study&nbsp;shows&nbsp;that the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme modifies the sodium storage performance, evidently confirming the important role of anionic chemistry in determining the electrochemical performance of the target electrode.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="cey2518-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="cey2518-sec-0020-title">2 EXPERIMENTAL SECTION</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="cey2518-sec-0030">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="cey2518-sec-0030-title">2.1 Materials</h3>
            
            <p>The HC was obtained from Guangdong Canrd New Energy Technology Co., Ltd. The NaPF<sub>6</sub>, NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>, NaBF<sub>4</sub>, NaClO<sub>4</sub>, NaTFSI, and diglyme with battery grade were purchased from Aladdin. Note that all the slats were further dried at 80°C overnight, and the residual H<sub>2</sub>O in the solvents employed was removed by the activated molecular sieve for 3 days.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="cey2518-sec-0040">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="cey2518-sec-0040-title">2.2 Electrode and electrolyte preparation</h3>
            
            <p>The HC, binder (sodium carboxymethyl cellulose), and conductive agent (Super P), with a mass ratio of 8:1:1, were mixed in deionized water to form a uniform slurry, and then the mixture was coated on the copper foil and further dried at 100°C overnight. Afterward, the working electrode with a diameter of 14 mm and mass loading of about 1.5 mg can be obtained after cutting. In addition, the NaPF<sub>6</sub>, NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>, NaBF<sub>4</sub>, NaClO<sub>4</sub>, and NaTFSI were dissolved in the diglyme to prepare the 1.0 M electrolyte. Based on the working electrode and electrolyte preparation, the coin-type (CR-2032) cells were assembled in the glovebox (oxygen content &lt; 0.1 ppm and water content &lt; 0.1 ppm), employing glass fiber and sodium foil as separator and counter electrode, respectively.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="cey2518-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="cey2518-sec-0050-title">2.3 Characterization</h3>
            
            <p>The characterizations of HC were conducted by field-emission scanning electron microscope (FESEM, Zeiss_Supra55) and X-ray diffractometer (D8 ADVANCE). The postmortem analyses of cycled electrodes, containing FESEM observation, high-resolution transmission electron microscope (HRTEM, Tecnai 12) observation, and X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) (ESCALAB 250Xi), were carried out after washing with the diglyme. Besides, the discharge/charge measurements of HC electrodes in various electrolytes were performed on LAND 2001A. The cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves of the HC electrode in different electrolytes at various scan rates were collected from an electrochemical workstation (CHI660B), and the electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) tests were conducted on the same workstation from 10<sup>−2</sup> to 10<sup>5</sup> Hz. The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) tests were measured using the battery test system with a pulse current density of 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> and a rest time of 1.0 h.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="cey2518-sec-0060">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="cey2518-sec-0060-title">3 RESULTS AND DISCUSSION</h2>
         
         <p>Taking HC as the mode electrode, a detailed investigation of electrochemical behaviors in ether-based electrolytes with various anions has been performed to determine the correlation between anionic chemistry and electrochemical behaviors. Commercial HC was employed in this study, with its corresponding FESEM and XRD pattern shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>. As shown, the HC particles, with no special morphology, exhibit an average size of about 10–20 μm, and the typical (002) and (100) planes can be clearly detected from the diffraction pattern.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0005_R_d148370241e597" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Adv Mater">5</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0012_R_d148370241e597" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Energy Storage Mater">12</a></sup></span> Herein, various conducting salt anions (PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>, BF<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>, CF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub><sup>−</sup>, ClO<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>, and TFSI<sup>−</sup>) dispersed in diglyme were selected as the model electrolytes. In principle, the different types of anions that participated in the solvation structure are believed to induce variations in terms of electrolyte stability, redox kinetics, and sodium storage behavior. Concerning the selection of ether solvent, both liner and cyclic ether solvents, including diglyme, 1,2-dimethoxyethane, triethylene glycol monomethyl ether, and tetrahydrofuran, have been employed as solvents for SIBs.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0024_R_d148370241e617" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem Sci">24</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0025_R_d148370241e617" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Chem Soc Rev">25</a></sup></span> In principle, the viscosity, compatibility with HC, dissolution ability for sodium salts, and ionic conductivity should be taken into consideration when selecting the solvent.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0005_R_d148370241e621" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Adv Mater">5</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0006_R_d148370241e621" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv Funct Mater">6</a></sup></span> Particularly, the high dissolution ability for sodium salts, excellent compatibility with HC, and modest viscosity, simultaneously receiving high ionic diffusion and good chemical stability, render the diglyme to be one of the promising ether solvents for HC.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0013_R_d148370241e624" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Energy Stor Mater">13</a></sup></span> A detailed investigation of these effects may offer deep insights into the interaction between electrode and electrolyte.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0015_R_d148370241e627" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Nano Energy">15</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0033_R_d148370241e627" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J Electrochem Soc">33</a></sup></span> In addition, the concentration of salt also shows a large influence on the inherent properties of electrolytes, especially for conductivity. An electrolyte with low concentration has limited charge carriers, which restricts the ion transference number, while the high viscosity in the electrolyte with high concentration impedes the ionic migration.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0034_R_d148370241e630" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Energy Stor Mater">34</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0035_R_d148370241e630" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J Power Sources">35</a></sup></span> Thus, taking both viscosity and conductivity into consideration, the concentration of electrolyte employed in this study is 1.0 M.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0003_R_d148370241e633" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Angew Chem Int Ed">3</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0026_R_d148370241e633" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Angew Chem Int Ed">26</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>It is worth noting that the HC electrodes in electrolytes containing NaClO<sub>4</sub> and NaTFSI depict serious fluctuations upon cycling, indicating significant decomposition of electrolytes (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>).<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0033_R_d148370241e643" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J Electrochem Soc">33</a></sup></span> Accordingly, the linear sweep voltammetry (LSV) curves (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>) of stainless steel|electrolyte|stainless steel cells from open-circuit voltage to 4.5 V show the discrepancy of electrochemical stability of various electrolytes, from where the oxidation current starts to rise at around 2.0 V for the NaClO<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaTFSI/diglyme. This demonstrates their poor antioxidation ability, and such results also reveal that the stability of diglyme-based electrolytes shows a large dependence on the anionic group employed.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0036_R_d148370241e652" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Angew Chem Int Ed">36</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0037_R_d148370241e652" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - J Mater Chem A">37</a></sup></span> Given this, the NaClO<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaTFSI/diglyme are excluded from this study, as their limited electrochemical behavior results in the failure of the HC electrode upon charging in these electrolytes.</p>
         
         <p>In principle, the correlation between anionic chemistry and electrochemical properties of electrolytes can be well built through the comparison of Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme and Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme-anion models (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0001">1A</a>) in the lowest unoccupied molecular orbital (LUMO) and reductive stability in a single-electron reduction reaction. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0001">1B</a>, all three models of Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme-PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>, Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme-BF<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>, and Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme-CF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub><sup>−</sup> demonstrate negative binding energies, thus demonstrating the high thermodynamic stability for the interaction between Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme and the anion.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0038_R_d148370241e691" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Angew Chem Int Ed">38</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0039_R_d148370241e691" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - ACS Energy Lett">39</a></sup></span> For different salt anions, the binding energies follow the order of CF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub><sup>−</sup> &lt; BF<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup> &lt; PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>. It is reasonable to understand such binding energy order since the anions in the Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme-anion solvation structure primarily interact with Na<sup>+</sup>, and the high electronegativity of F atoms in PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> induces the strong interaction.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0040_R_d148370241e714" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Batteries Supercaps">40</a></sup></span> Noting that the relatively higher binding energy between PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme complex allows more PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> to participate in the solvation structure, which may facilitate the subsequent decomposition of anion and formation of an inorganic-rich SEI.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0041_R_d148370241e726" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Angew Chem Int Ed">41</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cey2518-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/ded04f8c-04b0-452c-a723-c3936e55956b/cey2518-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/ded04f8c-04b0-452c-a723-c3936e55956b/cey2518-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/51d7e253-5b84-4aed-be80-d462b8bb012e/cey2518-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/ded04f8c-04b0-452c-a723-c3936e55956b/cey2518-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cey2518-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcey2.518" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">(A) Optimized geometric structures of Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme, Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme-PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>, Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme-BF<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>, and Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme-CF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub><sup>−</sup>. (B) Binding energies between the Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme and anions as well as the energy level change of the lowest unoccupied molecular orbital of anions and solvent before and after interacting of Na<sup>+</sup>-solvent complexes with anions. (C) Spin population values of anions in reduced Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme-anion complexes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>The effect of the anionic group on the stability of electrolytes was compared through the energy level change of the LUMO of anions and diglyme after introducing an anion into a Na<sup>+</sup> solvation sheath.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0040_R_d148370241e782" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Batteries Supercaps">40</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0041_R_d148370241e782" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Angew Chem Int Ed">41</a></sup></span> As depicted, the LUMO energy levels of anions in solvation structure decrease, while the LUMO energy levels of diglyme increase, hence manifesting the reduced reductive stability of anions and increased reductive stability of diglyme.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0038_R_d148370241e785" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Angew Chem Int Ed">38</a></sup></span> In principle, such variation can be generally ascribed to the electron-withdrawing effect of positively charged Na<sup>+</sup>, where the anions share the burden of the electron-withdrawing effect with the solvent, thus resulting in the reduced LUMO energy level of anions and increased LUMO energy level of diglyme.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0042_R_d148370241e790" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Nano Lett">42</a></sup></span> Further observation of the reductive stability of anions was performed through a single-electron reduction reaction. Specifically, a single electron was added to the Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme-anion complexes, and the distribution of this single unpaired electron is deduced from the spin population analysis, reflecting the electron affinity of species in the Na<sup>+</sup> solvation sheath.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0043_R_d148370241e798" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Nat Energy">43</a></sup></span> As seen from Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0001">1C</a>, the atoms of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>, BF<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup> and CF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub><sup>−</sup> in the solvation sheath occupy the majority of the single electron, meaning the electron aggregates around the anionic group, which in turn leads to the reduction of anions with the breaking of chemical bonds.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0044_R_d148370241e816" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Angew Chem Int Ed">44</a></sup></span> Specifically, for the CF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub><sup>−</sup>, the C, S, and O atoms share the electron, while most of the electron is aggregated at around the P and B atoms of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> and BF<sub>4</sub><sup>−</sup>, respectively, combined with the decreased reductive stability of the anionic group, which may result in breaking the P-F and B-F bonds, further leading to NaF-rich SEI layer.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0045_R_d148370241e831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Angew Chem Int Ed">45</a></sup></span> Of note, the NaF-rich SEI layer is believed to provide an efficient protection layer for the target electrode and accelerate the interfacial ionic diffusion, thereby contributing to high electrochemical sodium storage performance.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0027_R_d148370241e835" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Angew Chem Int Ed">27</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0028_R_d148370241e835" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Angew Chem Int Ed">28</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>To detect the variations of structure and components of the SEI layer with different anionic groups, XPS tests for the cycled HC electrodes were carried out. The SEI layers formed in the three electrolytes show similar compositions of C, O, F, and Na (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>), while the variations of peak intensities and binding energies can be observed in the corresponding high-resolution spectra. Specifically, the C 1s spectrum in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme exhibits three peaks at around 284.2, 284.7, and 286.1 eV (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0002">2A</a>), corresponding to C–C/C–H, C–O, and C═O of the organic species in SEI layer resulting from the solvent's decomposition, respectively.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0010_R_d148370241e848" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Energy Storage Mater">10</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0029_R_d148370241e848" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Chem Eng J">29</a></sup></span> The peak at 289.1 eV can be indexed to the inorganic Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>/Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>2</sub>R. For the O 1 s spectrum in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, obvious inorganic signals of O-F and Na-O at 536.4 and 531.2 eV, respectively, can be found owing to the reduction of NaPF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> solvent complex, while the peak at around 532.5 eV corresponds to the O–C and O–H species in SEI layer.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0011_R_d148370241e866" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Energy Storage Mater">11</a></sup></span> The two peaks in the F 1s spectrum can be ascribed to Na-F (683.7 eV) and the electrolyte salt (687.4 eV), and the Na-F bonds can be ascribed to the reductive decomposition of the PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0033_R_d148370241e872" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J Electrochem Soc">33</a></sup></span> Moreover, the existence of Na-F (NaF) and Na-O (Na<sub>2</sub>O) bonds can be confirmed by the deconvoluted peaks in the Na 1 s spectrum.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0015_R_d148370241e877" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Nano Energy">15</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cey2518-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/08cf5e94-8e08-4d53-86b2-5e8d022b380a/cey2518-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/08cf5e94-8e08-4d53-86b2-5e8d022b380a/cey2518-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/83264d02-5dc3-4744-8023-8fe3ece96d77/cey2518-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/08cf5e94-8e08-4d53-86b2-5e8d022b380a/cey2518-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cey2518-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcey2.518" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The XPS measurements for HC electrodes at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> after five&nbsp;cycles: (A) NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, (B) NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and (C) NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme. Percentages of the (D) C–C/C–H, (E) C–O, and (F) Na–F species in the SEI layers generated on HC electrodes in three electrolytes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>As shown, the C 1s, O 1s, F 1s, and Na 1s spectra for the cycled HC electrodes in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme exhibit similar fitting peaks, but the organic and inorganic species vary (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0002">2B,C</a>). Particularly, for NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme, the SEI layer contains a higher proportion of organic species (C–C, C–H, and C–O) but a lower proportion of inorganic species (Na–F and Na–O) compared with NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0002">2D–F</a>). This discrepancy can be attributed to the different stability of electrolytes with various anionic groups.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0046_R_d148370241e936" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J Mater Chem A">46</a></sup></span> Specifically, the comparison of inorganic/organic species in SEI layers formed in different electrolytes reveals that the SEI film generated in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme features the lowest contents (27.1% and 20.9%) of organic species (C–C/C–H, and C–O), followed by NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme (32.5% and 24.3%) and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme (36.2% and 31.8%). On the other hand, the content of Na-F in the SEI (15.2%) formed in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme is higher than those of the other two electrolytes. Accordingly, it can be deduced that the preferred decomposition of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> facilitates the generation of an inorganic-rich SEI.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0035_R_d148370241e954" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J Power Sources">35</a></sup></span> Previous studies<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0002_R_d148370241e957" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Nat Commun">2</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0047_R_d148370241e957" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Nat Commun">47</a></sup></span> have proved that the inorganic species in SEI can significantly improve its ionic conductivity, thus accelerating the interfacial charge transfer and reducing the diffusion barrier, and an appropriate higher content of inorganic species will also favor better electrochemical performance by suppressing the solubility of organic sodium carbonates (such as NaO<sub>2</sub>CO–C<sub>2</sub>H<sub>4</sub>–OCO<sub>2</sub>Na). Moreover, the inorganic species can also result in a high Young's modulus, contributing to high mechanical strength for the SEI layer.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0040_R_d148370241e969" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Batteries Supercaps">40</a></sup></span> Meanwhile, an appropriate content of organic species, coupling with the inorganic species, can induce high flexibility and elasticity to accommodate for the SEI layer to accommodate the large volume expansion and resist the side reactions.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0033_R_d148370241e972" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J Electrochem Soc">33</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>Furthermore, the observation of SEI layers formed in three electrolytes through HRTEM (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>) manifests that the thicknesses of SEI layers formed in NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme (27 nm) and NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme (20 nm) are slightly thicker than that of NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme (11 nm). This indicates that the PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> in diglyme is beneficial for the generation of a thinner SEI layer, which can avoid the continuous decomposition of electrolytes.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0011_R_d148370241e992" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Energy Storage Mater">11</a></sup></span> In brief, the thin and inorganic-rich SEI layer, formed in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, proves the preferred decomposition of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> upon electrochemical reduction, and highlights the excellent compatibility between NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme and the HC electrode, thereby contributing to modifying the interfacial charge transfer kinetics.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0004_R_d148370241e1003" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Carbon Energy">4</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0048_R_d148370241e1003" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv Funct Mater">48</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>In addition to the obvious effect of the anionic group on the electrochemical properties of electrolytes, the ionic migration behaviors are also influenced by the anion in electrolytes. Particularly, the comparison of Nyquist plots of the prepared electrolytes at room temperature based on the steel|electrolyte|steel cells reveals that the resistances of NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme are, respectively, 11.9, 10.5, and 9.7 Ω, which correspond to ionic conductivities of 2.9 × 10<sup>−4</sup>, 3.3 × 10<sup>−4</sup>, and 3.6 × 10<sup>−4</sup> S cm<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0003">3A,B</a>), according to Equation S1.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0018_R_d148370241e1028" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Small Methods">18</a></sup></span> As known, the high binding energy between Na<sup>+</sup> and the anionic group may induce the formation of ion pairs and aggregates, restricting the ionic conductivity, which becomes more serious in high concentrations.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0042_R_d148370241e1034" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Nano Lett">42</a></sup></span> Nevertheless, the low concentration of 1.0 M employed in this study can guarantee the efficient dissolution of salt in diglyme, thus leading to the slight discrepancy in ionic conductivity of the three electrolytes. Except for the ionic conductivity, the anionic group also shows a large impact on the ionic transference number in the electrolyte (Equation&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>). As seen from Figures&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0003">3C</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, the Na<sup>+</sup> transference number of NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme is determined to be 0.52, much higher than those of NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme (0.42) and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme (0.26). Combining the high binding energies between the Na<sup>+</sup>-diglyme and PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>, it can be deduced that the tight interaction of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>to the solvation structure impedes the migration of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>, and the restricted transference number of anionic group contributes to the high Na<sup>+</sup> transference number.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0049_R_d148370241e1071" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - J Power Sources">49</a></sup></span> In brief, the PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> in diglyme exhibits both satisfied ionic conductivity and high transference number, dramatically modifying the ionic migration and reducing concentration polarization in liquid electrolytes.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cey2518-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/8778a88b-460e-4aec-b30a-7efafa9b7d91/cey2518-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/8778a88b-460e-4aec-b30a-7efafa9b7d91/cey2518-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/83e84fca-2ba5-48a2-894d-4c4762c1ebd5/cey2518-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/8778a88b-460e-4aec-b30a-7efafa9b7d91/cey2518-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cey2518-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcey2.518" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">(A) Nyquist plots of three electrolytes based on steel|electrolyte|steel cells and (B) the calculated ionic conductivities. (C) Electrochemical determination of Na<sup>+</sup> transference number by combining a chronoamperometry experiment (DC voltage: 10 mV) with Nyquist plots (inset) for Na|electrolyte|Na cells before and after polarization in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme. (D) Comparison of discharge/charge profiles at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>. (E) Capacity contributions from the slope and plateau of the HC electrode in three electrolytes. (F) Summary of the initial Coulombic efficiency, plateau contribution, ionic conductivity, and Na<sup>+</sup> transference number of HC in three electrolytes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>To detect the effect of the anionic group for a detailed understanding of sodium storage behavior, CV measurements and galvanostatic discharge/charge tests were carried out. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, the sharp cathodic/anodic peaks at the low voltage around 0.1 V of the CV curves can be indexed to the reversible intercalation and deintercalation of Na<sup>+</sup>, and the slight variation between the first scan and the following scans reveals good electrochemical reversibility.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0048_R_d148370241e1116" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv Funct Mater">48</a></sup></span> Accordingly, the plateaus presented in discharge/charge profiles of HC in three electrolytes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0003">3D</a>) depict high consistency with the cathodic/anodic peaks. Specifically, the HC electrode exhibits initial discharge/charge capacities of 269.5/212.2, 233.6/174.0, and 187.6/140.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, acquiring initial Coulombic efficiencies of 78.7%, 74.5%, and 75.0%, in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme, respectively. In general, the preferred decomposition of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>-induced stable SEI abundant with inorganic species, combined with the fats mass transport in liquid electrolyte, restricts the decomposition of electrolyte, thus improving the initial capacity of HC in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0040_R_d148370241e1139" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Batteries Supercaps">40</a></sup></span> Generally, the rapid ionic migration kinetics-induced modified electrochemical reversibility accounts for the higher Coulombic efficiency of NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0050_R_d148370241e1144" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - J Mater Sci Technol">50</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0051_R_d148370241e1144" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - SusMat">51</a></sup></span> Importantly, the low capacity loss upon the initial cycle of HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme manifests not only the good interaction between electrode and electrolyte but also the restricted electrolyte decomposition, resulting from the robust and inorganic-rich SEI film.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0052_R_d148370241e1149" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Nano Energy">52</a></sup></span> Except for the specific capacity, the discharge/charge profiles of the HC electrode in three electrolytes are well-maintained, hence further highlighting the good compatibility of the HC electrode with diglyme.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0025_R_d148370241e1153" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Chem Soc Rev">25</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>Interestingly, detailed observation for the discharge/charge profiles demonstrates that the capacity contribution from slope and plateau varies with different anionic groups. As illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0003">3E</a>, the capacity contributions from the plateau are calculated to be 56.3%, 52.0%, and 46.2% in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme, respectively. In principle, the capacity from the plateau corresponds to the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation, and the high capacity contribution from the plateau in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme suggests convenient charge diffusion in bulk electrode, combined with the high ionic migration in liquid electrolyte mentioned above, which together guarantees rapid redox kinetics.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0038_R_d148370241e1174" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Angew Chem Int Ed">38</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0041_R_d148370241e1174" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Angew Chem Int Ed">41</a></sup></span> Accordingly, it can be concluded that the selection of anionic group not only shows an impact on the properties of electrolytes but also determines the sodium storage behaviors of the HC electrode.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0053_R_d148370241e1177" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Angew Chem">53</a></sup></span> Moreover, the schematic comparisons of initial Coulombic efficiency, plateau contribution, ionic conductivity, and Na<sup>+</sup> transference number in three electrolytes have been illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0003">3F</a>, from where the superiority of NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme is noticeable, thus revealing the excellent compatibility between NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme and HC with superior ionic migration dynamics in liquid electrolyte.</p>
         
         <p>The above analysis on reductive stability of electrolyte, component/structure of SEI layer, ionic migration in liquid electrolyte, and detailed sodium storage behavior has highlighted the advantage of NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme for HC electrode, but the investigation on the effect of anionic group for redox kinetics is insufficient. Based on the CV curves collected at various scan rates (Figures&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0004">4A</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>), the ionic diffusion kinetics in three electrolytes can be compared (Equation&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>).<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0050_R_d148370241e1204" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - J Mater Sci Technol">50</a></sup></span> After fitting the peak current versus the square root of the scan rate, the gradient can be used to determine the ionic diffusion kinetics in bulk electrodes.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0040_R_d148370241e1208" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Batteries Supercaps">40</a></sup></span> As illustrated (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0004">4B</a> and Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>), the absolute values of the slopes for the cathodic peaks were fitted to be 0.99, 0.91, and 0.83, respectively, for NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme, while the slopes for anodic peaks were 1.14, 0.55, and 0.54. This indicates that the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme features faster ionic diffusion kinetics than those in NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme, which is attributed to the high ionic migration in electrolyte and robust SEI layer abundant with inorganic species.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0016_R_d148370241e1234" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Nano Lett">16</a></sup></span> Further detailed comparison of ionic diffusion coefficients in three electrolytes through galvanostatic intermittent titration technology (Figures&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0004">4C</a> and&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>) depicts that the excellent compatibility between NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme and HC induces rapid Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion, showing higher average Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients than those of NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme. Noting that the coefficients at the plateau region are relatively lower compared with the slope region, thus demonstrating that the interaction is controlled by the diffusion behavior, and the high ionic dynamics of HC in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme can facilitate the charge transportation, resulting in modified electrochemical sodium storage performance.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0030_R_d148370241e1259" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Adv Energy Mater">30</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0039_R_d148370241e1259" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - ACS Energy Lett">39</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cey2518-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/34ad6c2b-3cef-4980-85dd-feb272fddb38/cey2518-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/34ad6c2b-3cef-4980-85dd-feb272fddb38/cey2518-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1666bc6a-c606-47da-a46f-250766bf5e6c/cey2518-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/34ad6c2b-3cef-4980-85dd-feb272fddb38/cey2518-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cey2518-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcey2.518" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">(A) CV curves with different scan rates, (B) fitted lines of peak current versus square root of scan rate, (C) GITT curves and calculated Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients, (D) Nyquist plots at various temperatures, and (E) Arrhenius plots of HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme. (F) Comparison of kinetics parameters of HC electrodes in three electrolytes.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>As demonstrated above, the NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme can induce the generation of an inorganic-rich SEI, hence reducing the charge-transfer barrier and promoting redox kinetics.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0054_R_d148370241e1291" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - ACS Energy Lett">54</a></sup></span> To verify this view, the EIS spectrum of HC electrodes under various temperatures in different electrolytes and corresponding fitted Arrhenius plots have been performed. For the NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0004">4D</a>), Nyquist plots ranging from −40°C to 20°C illustrate that the charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) at the middle-frequency region decreases gradually with an&nbsp;increase in temperature. This trend can be also found for NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>). The Arrhenius plots (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0004">4E</a>) obtained according to Equation S4 manifest that the energy barriers for charge transfer in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme are fitted to be 26.95, 35.60, and 66.31 meV, respectively.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0029_R_d148370241e1324" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Chem Eng J">29</a></sup></span> Generally, it is believed that the inherent high ionic migration kinetics in both electrolyte and electrode and robust SEI layer abundant with inorganic species contributes to the low energy barrier of charge transfer in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, which in turn facilitates the redox reaction and improves the battery performance.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0038_R_d148370241e1329" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Angew Chem Int Ed">38</a></sup></span> Also, the comparison of kinetics parameters in three electrolytes has been schematically illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0004">4F</a>, from where the NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme exhibits superiority in both ionic diffusion and charge transfer barrier. Further combined with the high Na<sup>+</sup> transference number and satisfied ionic conductivity in the liquid electrolyte, excellent sodium storage performance is deemed to be obtained.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0024_R_d148370241e1340" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem Sci">24</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <p>As depicted above, the superior compatibility between the HC electrode and NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme is evident from the characterizations and electrochemical measurements, where the high ionic migration in liquid electrolyte, rapid ionic diffusion in bulk electrode, and robust inorganic-rich SEI layer is believed to boost the sodium storage performance of the HC electrode. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0005">5A</a> illustrates the cycling performance of the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Obviously, the HC in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme displays higher specific capacity and better cycling stability than those of NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme. Particularly, after 100 cycles, the reversible capacities of the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> are 198.8, 175.9, and 138.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Besides, the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme exhibits higher and more stable Coulombic efficiencies compared with those in NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0005">5B</a>). Regarding the rate capability (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0005">5C</a>), the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme also outperforms the ones in NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme in terms of the specific capacities at all current densities, accompanied by well-maintained Coulombic efficiencies (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>). Specifically, the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme exhibits reversible capacities of 206.5, 190.1, 182.3, 172.3, and 161.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with current density increases of 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 3.0, and 4.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, showing superior rate capability. Additionally, compared with the gradually degraded plateau region in NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme (Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>), the rate profiles of HC in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme are well maintained (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0005">5D</a>), manifesting modified electrochemical polarization, which thus results in higher specific capacities delivered by the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme than the other electrolytes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0005">5E</a>).<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0055_R_d148370241e1437" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Chem Eng J">55</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cey2518-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/b343ebb9-c74f-4116-aa95-c67c43cbef7b/cey2518-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/b343ebb9-c74f-4116-aa95-c67c43cbef7b/cey2518-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/8491dba1-948b-4f5e-ac65-cf22dcf5809a/cey2518-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/b343ebb9-c74f-4116-aa95-c67c43cbef7b/cey2518-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cey2518-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcey2.518" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The comparison of sodium storage performance of HC electrode in three electrolytes: (A) cycling at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, (B) Coulombic efficiencies, and (C) rate capability. (D) Rate profiles of HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme. (E) Comparison of rate capabilities of HC in three electrolytes. (F) Long-term cycling of HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme at 4.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Ex-situ Raman spectra of HC in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme upon (G) discharge and (H) charge.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>The comparison of the long-term cycling performance of HC at 4.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> in three electrolytes has been shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0005">5F</a>, where a higher specific capacity of 182.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> can be obtained in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, outperforming those of NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme. Besides, the superiority of the Coulombic efficiencies of HC in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme over those of NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>. Such ultra-stable sodium storage performance can be mainly ascribed to the rapid redox kinetics, fast interfacial charge transfer, and superior interaction between electrode and electrolyte.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0034_R_d148370241e1501" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Energy Stor Mater">34</a></sup></span> To get a deep understanding of the excellent sodium storage performance of the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, ex-situ Raman spectra measurements at selected voltages were performed. For the discharging, the peak intensity of the D band gradually broadens and decreases from the open circuit voltage to 1.0 V, while the peak position maintains well upon the initial discharge.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0056_R_d148370241e1506" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Adv Energy Mater">56</a>, <a href="#cey2518-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0057_R_d148370241e1506" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Adv Funct Mater">57</a></sup></span> Further discharging to 0.05 V results in the left shifting of the G band and the disappearance of the D band, thus confirming the intercalation of sodium ions into the carbon layers and filling of nanopores.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0058_R_d148370241e1509" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - ACS Energy Lett">58</a></sup></span> Regarding the reverse charging, the G band shows a gradual shift toward&nbsp;the right, and the D band appears again with the process of charging depth.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0056_R_d148370241e1512" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Adv Energy Mater">56</a></sup></span> In brief, the reversible variations of G and D bands of HC in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme demonstrate that the excellent electrode/electrolyte interaction induces excellent electrochemical reversibility, thus contributing to stable cycling and high energy output.</p>
         
         <p>To further understand the inherent effect of salt anion on the compatibility between electrode and electrolyte, FESEM investigations on the HC electrode after cycling in three electrolytes were conducted (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0006">6A–F</a>). After 50 and 100 cycles, the corrosion of electrolytes to the electrode is evident for all three electrolytes. Even so, the HC particles can still be observed for the NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, while no HC can be detected in NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme, revealing good compatibility between HC and NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme. Compared with the smooth surface of the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, the surfaces of the HC electrode in NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme and NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme become much rougher, which may increase the ionic diffusion length and cause increased electrochemical polarization.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0057_R_d148370241e1543" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Adv Funct Mater">57</a></sup></span> As known, the charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) is a typical index to estimate the interfacial kinetics, and the comparison of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> for the HC electrodes in three electrolytes with different cycling numbers further reveals their discrepancies in interfacial behaviors. As illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#cey2518-fig-0006">6G–I</a>, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values of HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme are well-maintained and kept at relatively low values around 9.0 Ω, showing little dependence on the cycling number, which mainly results from the favorable interaction between electrode and electrolyte, rapid ionic kinetics, and stable SEI layer rich&nbsp;with&nbsp;inorganic species.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0003_R_d148370241e1562" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Angew Chem Int Ed">3</a></sup></span> For the NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, despite the low <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value after 10 cycles, the value gradually increases to 13 and 19 Ω after 50 and 100 cycles, respectively. In regard to the NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values show a large increase with the increase of cycling number, with values of 15, 78, and 138 Ω, after 10, 50, and 100 cycles, respectively. The gradual increase in <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of HC electrode in NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme is attributed to the high energy barrier at the interface for charge transfer, restricted ionic migration kinetics in liquid electrolyte and bulk electrode, and relatively thick SEI layer, which should also be responsible for its unsatisfactory electrochemical sodium storage performance.<span><sup><a href="#cey2518-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="cey2518-bib-0015_R_d148370241e1586" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Nano Energy">15</a></sup></span></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="cey2518-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/a4bf5479-7259-42f5-ac9b-de39fef00d8c/cey2518-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/a4bf5479-7259-42f5-ac9b-de39fef00d8c/cey2518-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/dabd472e-e55f-44de-971d-b6d2a2a99242/cey2518-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/a4bf5479-7259-42f5-ac9b-de39fef00d8c/cey2518-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=cey2518-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fcey2.518" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">FESEM images of HC electrodes in (A, B) NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, (C, D) NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and (E, F) NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme after 50 and 100 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Nyquist plots of HC electrode after various cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup> in (G) NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme, (H) NaBF<sub>4</sub>/diglyme, and (I) NaSO<sub>3</sub>CF<sub>3</sub>/diglyme (the insets are the equivalent circuit models).</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="cey2518-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="cey2518-sec-0070-title">4 CONCLUSION</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, this work presents a comprehensive study on the influence of the anionic group in diglyme for the HC electrode on the stability of the electrolyte, component/structure of the SEI layer, redox kinetics, and electrochemical sodium storage performance. The significant role of anionic chemistry in determining the properties of electrolytes and electrochemical behaviors has been clarified. Generally, the preferred decomposition of F-containing anionic group with low reductive stability will result in the generation of inorganic-rich SEI, and the excellent compatibility between the salt and solvent can induce high ionic kinetics, contributing to reducing the electrochemical polarization and modifying the electrochemical performance. Specifically, the excellent compatibility between NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme and HC, combined with the reduced reductive stability of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>, induces the preferred decomposition of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup>and formation of inorganic-rich SEI, simultaneously resulting in remarkable ionic kinetics in terms of high Na<sup>+</sup> transference number, low energy barrier upon charge transfer, and large ionic diffusion coefficient. Accordingly, these excellent features confer the HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>/diglyme with excellent sodium storage performance. More importantly, this work highlights the significance of the rational selection of salt anion in ether-based electrolytes to achieve high performance with robust rate capability and cycling stability for HC electrodes.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
